We were incorporated under the laws of the State of Colorado on January 12
 2000 under the name Capital Resources Alliance
 Inc. &nbsp;At inception
 we were a development stage company in the business of mining and exploration.&nbsp; On May 19
 2014 our company completed a reverse merger with Nate&rsquo;s Pancakes
 Inc.
 an Indiana company
 with Nate&rsquo;s Pancakes being the surviving entity.&nbsp; In May 2014
 we changed our name from Capital Resource Alliance
In connection with the reverse merger
 we became a food manufacturing and product company
 and in May 2014
 we executed a licensing agreement with Nate&rsquo;s Pancakes to market and sell &ldquo;Nate&rsquo;s Homemade&rdquo;
We are an &ldquo;emerging growth company&rdquo; as defined under the Jumpstart Our Business Startups Act
 commonly referred to as the JOBS Act. We will remain an &ldquo;emerging growth company&rdquo; for up to five years
 or until the earliest of (i) the last day of the first fiscal year in which our total annual gross revenues exceed $1 billion
 (ii) the date that we become a &ldquo;large accelerated filer&rdquo; as defined in Rule 12b-2 under the Securities Exchange Act of 1934
As an &ldquo;emerging growth company
&rdquo; we may take advantage of certain exemptions from various reporting requirements that are applicable to other public companies that are not &ldquo;emerging growth companies&rdquo; including
not being required to comply with the auditor attestation requirements of section404(b) of the Sarbanes-Oxley Act (we also will not be subject to the auditor attestation requirements of Section404(b) as long as we are a &ldquo;smaller reporting company
In addition
 Section 107 of the JOBS Act provides that an &ldquo;emerging growth company&rdquo; can take advantage of the extended transition period provided in Section&nbsp;7(a)(2)(B) of the Securities Act for complying with new or revised accounting standards. Under this provision
 an &ldquo;emerging growth company&rdquo; can delay the adoption of certain accounting standards until those standards would otherwise apply to private companies. In other words
 an &ldquo;emerging growth company&rdquo; can delay the adoption of such accounting standards until those standards would otherwise apply to private companies until the first to occur of the date the subject company (i) is no longer an &ldquo;emerging growth company&rdquo; or (ii) affirmatively and irrevocably opts out of the extended transition period provided in Securities Act Section 7(a) (2) (B). Our company has elected to take advantage of this extended transition period and
 as a result
 our financial statements may not be comparable to the financial statements of other public companies. Accordingly
 until the date that we are no longer an &ldquo;emerging growth company&rdquo; or affirmatively and irrevocably opt out of the exemption provided by Securities Act Section 7(a) (2) (B)
 upon the issuance of a new or revised accounting standard that applies to your financial statements and has a different effective date for public and private companies

We operate in a highly competitive environment.&nbsp;We have numerous competitors of varying sizes
 including manufacturers of private label products
 as well as manufacturers of other branded food products
 which compete for trade merchandising support and consumer dollars. We compete with large conventional consumer packaged foods companies. We also compete with natural and organic consumer packaged foods companies.&nbsp; At present
Competitive factors in our industry include product innovation
 product quality
 price
 brand recognition and loyalty
 product variety and ingredients
 product packaging and package design
 effectiveness of marketing and promotional activity
As a manufacturer and distributor of food products
 we are subject to a number of food-related regulations
 including the Federal Food
 Drug and Cosmetic Act and regulations promulgated thereunder by the FDA.&nbsp;This comprehensive regulatory framework governs the manufacture (including composition and ingredients)
 labeling
 packaging
regulates holding
specifies the standards of identity for certain foods
In March 2014
 the FDA issued a proposed rule that would make significant changes to the information appearing in
 and the format of
 the nutrition facts appearing on food labels. In July 2015
 the FDA issued a supplemental proposed rule to establish a reference value for added sugars and to require a declaration of the percent daily value of added sugars on the food label. The proposed rule would also revise the footnote in the nutrition label regarding the percent daily value. It is not clear whether FDA will issue final regulation or
 if it does
In addition
 the FDA enforces the Public Health Service Act and regulations issued thereunder
 which authorizes regulatory activity necessary to prevent the introduction
 transmission
 or spread of communicable diseases. These regulations require
 for example
 pasteurization of milk and milk products. The FDA also is implementing the Food Safety Modernization Act of 2011 (FSMA) which
 among other things
 mandates that the FDA adopt preventive controls to be implemented by farms
 warehouses
In September 2015
 FDA released final rules implementing the Produce Safety and Current Good Manufacturing Practices
 Hazard Analysis and Risk Based Preventive Controls (HARPC) requirements for human food and animal food
 which was a major milestone in the implementation of FSMA. The final rules revise the FDA&rsquo;s food safety regulations by: (1)&nbsp;codifying good agricultural practices and water fertilizer action limits
 (2) updating and revising certain requirements in the existing current good manufacturing practices regulations (current 21 CFR Part 110)
 (3) requiring the establishment and implementation of a food safety system that includes an analysis of hazards and risk-based preventive controls and sets requirements for a written food safety plan
 and (4) adding new requirements for a risk-based end-to-end supply chain program. Compliance is required by September 19
 2016
 with respect to the new good manufacturing practices and HARPC regulations
 and by January 2017
We are subject to numerous other federal
 state
 and local regulations involving such matters as the licensing and registration of manufacturing facilities
 enforcement by government health agencies of standards for our products
 inspection of our facilities
 and regulation of our trade practices in connection with the sale of our products. In response to food-borne illness events
 FDA scrutiny of the food and beverage industry has increased over the past few years
We are subject to various labeling requirements with respect to our products at the federal
 state
 and local levels. At the federal level
 the FDA has authority to review product labeling
 and the Federal Trade Commission may review labeling and advertising materials
 including online and television advertisements to determine if advertising materials are misleading. Similarly
 many states review dairy product labels to determine whether they comply with applicable state laws. In addition
 the European Union has issued and enforces rules governing foodstuff labeling
 nutrition

Long-lived assets such as property and equipment are stated at their fair value acquisition cost and reviewed for impairment whenever facts and circumstances indicate that the carrying value may not be recoverable. The Company applies Topic 718 &ldquo;Share-Based Payments&rdquo; (&ldquo;Topic 718&rdquo;) to share-based compensation
The Company accounts for equity-based transactions with non-employees under the provisions of ASC Topic No. 505-50
 &ldquo;Equity-Based Payments to Non-Employees&rdquo; (&ldquo;Topic No. 505-50&rdquo;). Topic No. 505-50 establishes that equity-based payment transactions with non-employees shall be measured at the fair value of the consideration received or the fair value of the equity instruments issued
It is the company&rsquo;s policy that revenues and gains will be recognized in accordance with ASC Topic 605-10-25
 &ldquo;Revenue Recognition.&rdquo; Under ASC Topic 605-10-25
 revenue earning activities are recognized upon the sale and delivery of its products. As of May 31

The Company uses the asset and liability method of accounting for income taxes in accordance with ASC 740-10
 &ldquo;Accounting for Income Taxes.&rdquo; Under this method
 income tax expense is recognized for the amount of: (i) taxes payable or refundable for the current year; and
 (ii) deferred tax consequences of temporary differences resulting from matters that have been recognized in an entity&rsquo;s financial statements or tax returns. Deferred tax assets and liabilities are measured using enacted tax rates expected to apply to taxable income in the years in which those temporary differences are expected to be recovered or settled. The effect on deferred tax assets and liabilities of a change in tax rates is recognized in the results of operations in the period that includes the enactment date. A valuation allowance is provided to reduce the deferred tax assets reported if
 based on the weight of available positive and negative evidence
ASC 740-10 prescribes a recognition threshold and measurement attribute for the financial statement recognition of a tax position taken or expected to be taken on a tax return. Under ASC 740-10
 a tax benefit from an uncertain tax position taken or expected to be taken may be recognized only if it is &ldquo;more likely than not&rdquo; that the position is sustainable upon examination
 based on its technical merits. The tax benefit of a qualifying position under ASC 740-10 would equal the largest amount of tax benefit that is greater than 50% likely of being realized upon ultimate settlement with a taxing authority having full knowledge of all the relevant information. A liability (including interest and penalties
 if applicable) is established to the extent a current benefit has been recognized on a tax return for matters that are considered contingent upon the outcome of an uncertain tax position. Related interest and penalties
 if any

Long-lived assets such as property and equipment are stated at their fair value acquisition cost and reviewed for impairment whenever facts and circumstances indicate that the carrying value may not be recoverable. Amortization of long-lived assets are calculated by the straight line method over their estimated useful lives. When required impairment losses on assets to be held and used are recognized based on the fair value of the asset. The fair value is determined based on estimates of future cash flows
 market value of similar assets
 if available
 or independent appraisals
 if required. If the carrying amount of the long-lived asset is not recoverable from its undiscounted cash flows
 an impairment loss is recognized for the difference between the carrying amount and fair value of the asset. When fair values are not available
For federal income tax purposes
 depreciation is computed under the modified accelerated cost recovery system. For financial statements purposes

The Company adopted ASC Topic 820

 which defines fair value
 establishes a framework for measuring fair value

The standard provides a consistent definition of fair value which focuses on an exit price that would be received upon sale of an asset or paid to transfer a liability in an orderly transaction between market participants at the measurement date. The Company computes net income (loss) per share in accordance with Accounting Standards Codification (&ldquo;ASC&rdquo;) 260
. ASC 260 requires presentation of both basic and diluted earnings per share (EPS) on the face of the income statement. Basic EPS is computed by dividing net income (loss) available to common shareholders (numerator) by the weighted average number of shares outstanding (denominator) during the period. Diluted EPS gives effect to all dilutive potential common shares outstanding during the period using the treasury stock method and convertible preferred stock using the if-converted method. In computing diluted EPS
 the average stock price for the period is used in determining the number of shares assumed to be purchased from the exercise of stock options or warrants. Diluted EPS excludes all dilutive potential shares if their effect is anti-dilutive. There were 4

In November 2015
 the FASB issued (ASU) 2015-17
 &ldquo;Balance Sheet Classification of Deferred Taxes.&rdquo; Currently deferred taxes for each tax jurisdiction are presented as a net current asset or liability and net noncurrent asset or liability on the balance sheet. To simplify the presentation
 the new guidance requires that deferred tax liabilities and assets for all jurisdictions along with any related valuation allowances be classified as noncurrent in a classified statement of financial position. This guidance is effective for interim and annual reporting periods beginning after December 15
 2016
 and early adoption is permitted. The Company has adopted this guidance in the fourth quarter of the year ended December 31
 2015 on a retrospective basis. The adoption of this guidance did not have a material impact on the Company&rsquo;s financial position
 results of operations or cash flows
Recent Accounting Pronouncements Issued But Not Adopted as of May 31
In March 2016
 the FASB issued ASU 2016-09
 &ldquo;Compensation - Stock Compensation (Topic 718): Improvements to Employee Share-Based Payment Accounting&rdquo;. The amendments are effective for public companies for annual periods beginning after December 15
 2016
 and interim periods within those annual periods. Several aspects of the accounting for share-based payment award transactions are simplified
In February 2016
 the FASB issued ASU No. 2016-02
 &ldquo;Leases (Topic 842)&rdquo; (&ldquo;ASU 2016-02&rdquo;). ASU 2016-02 requires an entity to recognize assets and liabilities arising from a lease for both financing and operating leases. The ASU will also require new qualitative and quantitative disclosures to help investors and other financial statement users better understand the amount
 timing
 and uncertainty of cash flows arising from leases. ASU 2016-02 is effective for fiscal years beginning after December 15
 2018
In January 2016
 the FASB issued ASU 2016-01
 which amends the guidance in U.S. GAAP on the classification and measurement of financial instruments. Changes to the current guidance primarily affect the accounting for equity investments
 financial liabilities under the fair value option
 and the presentation and disclosure requirements for financial instruments. In addition
 the ASU clarifies guidance related to the valuation allowance assessment when recognizing deferred tax assets resulting from unrealized losses on available-for-sale debt securities. The new standard is effective for fiscal years and interim periods beginning after December 15
 2017
 and upon adoption
In September 2015
 the FASB issued ASU 2015-16
 &ldquo;Simplifying the Accounting for Measurement &#8211;Period Adjustments.&rdquo; Changes to the accounting for measurement-period adjustments relate to business combinations. Currently
 an acquiring entity is required to retrospectively adjust the balance sheet amounts of the acquiree recognized at the acquisition date with a corresponding adjustment to goodwill as a result of changes made to the balance sheet amounts of the acquiree. The measurement period is the period after the acquisition date during which the acquirer may adjust the balance sheet amounts recognized for a business combination (generally up to one year from the date of acquisition). The changes eliminate the requirement to make such retrospective adjustments
 and
 instead require the acquiring entity to record these adjustments in the reporting period they are determined. The new standard is effective for both public and private companies for periods beginning after December 15
In August 2015
 the FASB issued ASU No. 2015-14
In April 2015, the FASB issued ASU 2015-05, Intangibles - Goodwill and Other - Internal-Use Software (Subtopic 350-40): Customer's Accounting for Fees Paid in a Cloud Computing Arrangement
In April 2015, the FASB issued ASU 2015-03, Interest - Imputation of Interest (Subtopic 835-30): Simplifying the Presentation of Debt Issuance Costs

 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;On October 8, 2015, the Company issued a Promissory&#13;Note (the &amp;#147;Note&amp;#148;) to Tarpon Bay Partners LLC, for $50,000, due April 30, 2016. The Note carries an annual interest&#13;rate of 10%. As of May 31, 2016, the Company owes $53,517, of which $3,517 is accrued interest. The Company recorded $50,000 to&#13;additional paid in capital, as the Note is to secure equity financing. The note is currently in maturity default.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;i&gt;Vista Capital&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;On March 27, 2015, the Company received financing&#13;in the amount of $110,000 from Vista Capital Investments, LLC, sold to BOU Trust on September 29, 2015. The Company expected to&#13;pay off the amount within 90 days from its receipt bearing 10% interest, mature in two years, at any time on or after the issuance&#13;date, the holder shall be entitled to convert any portion of the outstanding and unpaid conversion amount in to fully paid and&#13;non-assessable shares of Common Stock. The Company could repay the note within 90 days with no prepayment penalty and within 180&#13;days with a prepayment penalty equal to 10% of the balance. Conversion price was 65% of the lowest trade occurring during the 20&#13;consecutive trading days immediately preceding the conversion date. On September 29, 2015, the Company entered into the agreement&#13;of exchange notes with Vista and BOU trust. BOU trust purchased $121,000 of principal amount and accrued interest and the reminder&#13;of note of $12,222 was exchanged for warrant for Vista. As a result of this agreement, the conversion price was amended to 60%&#13;of the lowest traded price for 20 trading days prior to conversion. On October 20, 2015, the Company entered into the agreement&#13;of exchange notes with BOU trust and RDW Capital, LLC. RDW Capital, LLC purchased $35,600 of a portion of $121,000 convertible&#13;note. During the year ended May, 2016, the notes of $121,000 were converted into 32,534,420 shares of common stock. The note was&#13;discounted for a derivative (see note 7 for details) and the discount is being amortized over the life of the note using the effective&#13;interest method resulting in $100,205 of interest expense for the year ended May 31, 2016.&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;i&gt;Typenex Co&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;On July 24, 2015, the Company received financing&#13;in the amount of $93,000 from TypenexCo-Investment, LLC with $13,000 cash discount to the lender and incurred $8,000 financing&#13;costs to third parties. The deferred financing cost is being amortized over the life of the note using the effective interest method&#13;resulting in $8,000 of interest expense for the year ended May 31, 2016. The $93,000 bears an 8% interest and matures in nine months.&#13;The holder shall be entitled to convert any portion of the outstanding and unpaid conversion amount in to fully paid and non-assessable&#13;shares of Common Stock. Conversion price is 50% of the average of the three lowest closing bid prices for the 15 previous consecutive&#13;trading days prior to the payment date. The Company may prepay the note at any time at an amount equal to 120% of the outstanding&#13;principal and the accrued and unpaid interest. The note was discounted for a derivative (see note 7 for details) and the discount&#13;is being amortized over the life of the note using the effective interest method resulting in $93,000 of interest expense for the&#13;year ended May 31, 2016. During the year ended May 31, 2016, the notes of $53,312 were converted into 48,150,000 shares of common&#13;stock.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;i&gt;EMA Financial&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;On August 14, 2015, the Company received financing&#13;in the amount of $65,500 from EMA Financial, LLC with $5,500 cash discount to the lender and incurred $6,000 financing costs to&#13;third parties. The deferred financing cost is being amortized over the life of the note using the effective interest method resulting&#13;in $4,915 of interest expense for year ended May 31, 2016. The $65,500 bears 10% interest and matures in twelve months. The holder&#13;shall be entitled to convert any portion of the outstanding and unpaid conversion amount in to fully paid and non-assessable shares&#13;of Common Stock. Conversion price is the less of closing sale price of $0.035 and 60% of the lowest trade occurring during the&#13;15 consecutive trading days immediately preceding the conversion date. The Company may prepay the note at any time during the first&#13;120 days, at an amount equal to 125% of the outstanding principal and the accrued and unpaid interest, but no prepayment permitted&#13;thereafter. The note was discounted for a derivative (see note 7 for details) and the discount is being amortized over the life&#13;of the note using the effective interest method resulting in $58,336 of interest expense for the year ended May 31, 2016. During&#13;the year ended May 31, 2016, the notes of $25,533 were converted into 36,976,671 shares of common stock.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;On September 25, 2015, the Company received&#13;financing in the amount of $68,250 from BOU Trust with $3,250 cash discount to the lender and incurred $6,500 financing costs to&#13;third parties. The deferred financing cost is being amortized over the life of the note using the effective interest method resulting&#13;in $6,500 of interest expense for the year ended May 31, 2016. The $68,250 bears 10% interest and matures on March 25, 2016. The&#13;holder shall be entitled to convert any portion of the outstanding and unpaid conversion amount in to fully paid and non-assessable&#13;shares of Common Stock. Conversion price is the 60% of the lowest traded price, determined on the then current trading market for&#13;the Company&amp;#146;s common stock, for the 20 trading days prior to conversion. The Company may prepay any portion of the principal&#13;amount at 130% of such amount along with any accrued interest of this note at any time upon send days written notice to the holder.&#13;The note was discounted for a derivative (see note 7 for details) and the discount is being amortized over the life of the note&#13;using the effective interest method resulting in $68,250 of interest expense for the year ended May 31, 2016. During the year ended&#13;May 31, 2016, the notes of $7,990 were converted into 11,097,800 shares of common stock.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;On November 5, 2015, the Company issued convertible&#13;note of $30,000 to Lucosky Brookman, LLC. The Company repays in advance $5,000 per month. The $30,000 bears 0% interest and matures&#13;on March 20, 2016. The holder shall be entitled to convert any portion of the outstanding and unpaid conversion amount in to fully&#13;paid and non-assessable shares of Common Stock. Conversion price is the 60% of average of the lowest for 10 trading days prior&#13;to conversion at the option of the Holder, in whole at any time and from time to time. During the year ended May 31, 2016, the&#13;notes of $10,000 were repaid. Upon the later of the Maturity Date or that date which is six months following the date hereof, this&#13;Note shall be convertible into shares of the Company&amp;#146;s common stock. The note was discounted for a derivative (see note 7&#13;for details) and the discount was amortized over the life of the note using the effective interest method resulting in $20,000&#13;of interest expense for the year ended May 31, 2016.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;i&gt;Fourth Man, LLC&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;On November 5, 2015, the Company received financing&#13;in the amount of $55,000 from Fourth Man, LLC, with $5,000 cash discount to the lender and incurred $4,000 financing costs to third&#13;parties. The deferred financing cost is being amortized over the life of the note using the effective interest method resulting&#13;in $3,048 of interest expense for the year end May 31, 2016. The $55,000 bears 10% interest and matures on August 4, 2016. The&#13;holder shall be entitled to convert any portion of the outstanding and unpaid conversion amount in to fully paid and non-assessable&#13;shares of Common Stock. Conversion price is the 53% of the lowest daily trading price, determined on the then current trading market&#13;for the Company&amp;#146;s common stock, for 10 trading days prior to conversion at the option of the Holder, in whole at any time&#13;and from time to time. During the first 90 days subsequent to the date of issuance, the company may prepay any portion of the principal&#13;amount at 130% of such amount along with any accrued interest of this debenture at any time upon seven days written notice to the&#13;holder. After the first 90 days subsequent to the date of issuance, the company may prepay any portion of the principal amount&#13;at 150% of such amount along with any accrued interest of this debenture at any time upon seven days written notice to the holder.&#13;The note was discounted for a derivative (see note 7 for details) and the discount is being amortized over the life of the note&#13;using the effective interest method resulting in $41,905 of interest expense for the year ended May 31, 2016.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Summary of significant accounting policies&#13;of Nate&amp;#146;s Food Co. (the &amp;#147;Company&amp;#148;) is presented to assist in understanding the Company&amp;#146;s financial statements.&#13;The accounting policies presented in these footnotes conform to accounting principles generally accepted in the United States of&#13;America and have been consistently applied in the preparation of the accompanying financial statements. These financial statements&#13;and notes are representations of the Company&amp;#146;s management who are responsible for their integrity and objectivity.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Our Company&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Nate&amp;#146;s Food Co. (&amp;#147;we&amp;#148;, &amp;#147;us&amp;#148;,&#13;&amp;#147;our&amp;#148;, the &amp;#34;Company&amp;#34; or the &amp;#34;Registrant&amp;#34;) was incorporated in the state of Colorado on January&#13;12, 2000. Nate&amp;#146;s Food Co. is domiciled in the state of Colorado, and its corporate headquarters are located in Huntington&#13;Beach, California. The Company selected May 31 as its fiscal year end. On May 12, 2014, Nate&amp;#146;s Pancakes Inc. was incorporated&#13;in the state of Indiana. On May 19, 2014, the Company completed a reverse merger between with Nate&amp;#146;s Pancakes, Inc. Nate&amp;#146;s&#13;Pancakes was the surviving Company. In May 2014, the Company changed its name from Capital Resource Alliance to Nate&amp;#146;s Food&#13;Co.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;u&gt;Use of Estimates&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The preparation of financial statements in&#13;accounting principles generally accepted in the United States of America requires management to make estimates and assumptions&#13;that affect the reported amounts of assets and liabilities and disclosure of contingent assets and liabilities at the date of the&#13;financial statements and the reported amounts of revenues and expenses during the reporting period. A change in managements&amp;#146;&#13;estimates or assumptions could have a material impact on Nate&amp;#146;s Food Co. financial condition and results of operations during&#13;the period in which such changes occurred. Actual results could differ from those estimates. Nate&amp;#146;s Food Co.&amp;#146;s financial&#13;statements reflect all adjustments that management believes are necessary for the fair presentation of their financial condition&#13;and results of operations for the periods presented.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;u&gt;Cash and Cash Equivalents&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;For purposes of the statement of cash flows,&#13;the Company considers all short-term debt securities purchased with maturity of three months or less to be cash equivalents.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;u&gt;Share-Based Compensation&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company applies Topic 718 &amp;#147;Share-Based&#13;Payments&amp;#148; (&amp;#147;Topic 718&amp;#148;) to share-based compensation, which requires the measurement of the cost of services received&#13;in exchange for an award of an equity instrument based on the grant-date fair value of the award. Compensation cost is recognized&#13;when the event occurs. The Black-Scholes option-pricing model is used to estimate the fair value of options granted.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company accounts for equity-based transactions&#13;with non-employees under the provisions of ASC Topic No. 505-50, &amp;#147;Equity-Based Payments to Non-Employees&amp;#148; (&amp;#147;Topic&#13;No. 505-50&amp;#148;). Topic No. 505-50 establishes that equity-based payment transactions with non-employees shall be measured at&#13;the fair value of the consideration received or the fair value of the equity instruments issued, whichever is more reliably measurable.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;u&gt;Revenue Recognition&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;It is the company&amp;#146;s policy that revenues&#13;and gains will be recognized in accordance with ASC Topic 605-10-25, &amp;#147;Revenue Recognition.&amp;#148; Under ASC Topic 605-10-25,&#13;revenue earning activities are recognized upon the sale and delivery of its products. As of May 31, 2016 and 2015, the Company&#13;has generated $29,250 and $3,996 in revenue. Consideration received prior to our delivery of the product is deferred until delivery.&#13;We had $0 and $29,250 in deferred revenue for a deposit from a related party as of May 31, 2016 and 2015, respectively. See footnote&#13;3 for details.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;u&gt;Income Taxes&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company uses the asset and liability method&#13;of accounting for income taxes in accordance with ASC 740-10, &amp;#147;Accounting for Income Taxes.&amp;#148; Under this method, income&#13;tax expense is recognized for the amount of: (i) taxes payable or refundable for the current year; and, (ii) deferred tax consequences&#13;of temporary differences resulting from matters that have been recognized in an entity&amp;#146;s financial statements or tax returns.&#13;Deferred tax assets and liabilities are measured using enacted tax rates expected to apply to taxable income in the years in which&#13;those temporary differences are expected to be recovered or settled. The effect on deferred tax assets and liabilities of a change&#13;in tax rates is recognized in the results of operations in the period that includes the enactment date. A valuation allowance is&#13;provided to reduce the deferred tax assets reported if, based on the weight of available positive and negative evidence, it is&#13;more likely than not that some portion or all of the deferred tax assets will not be realized.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;ASC 740-10 prescribes a recognition threshold&#13;and measurement attribute for the financial statement recognition of a tax position taken or expected to be taken on a tax return.&#13;Under ASC 740-10, a tax benefit from an uncertain tax position taken or expected to be taken may be recognized only if it is &amp;#147;more&#13;likely than not&amp;#148; that the position is sustainable upon examination, based on its technical merits. The tax benefit of a qualifying&#13;position under ASC 740-10 would equal the largest amount of tax benefit that is greater than 50% likely of being realized upon&#13;ultimate settlement with a taxing authority having full knowledge of all the relevant information. A liability (including interest&#13;and penalties, if applicable) is established to the extent a current benefit has been recognized on a tax return for matters that&#13;are considered contingent upon the outcome of an uncertain tax position. Related interest and penalties, if any, are included as&#13;components of income tax expense and income taxes payable.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;u&gt;Research and Development&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;We employ processes at our principal manufacturing&#13;locations that emphasize applied research and technical services directed at product improvement and quality control. In addition,&#13;we conduct research activities related to the development of new products. Research and development expense was $1,850 and $105,232&#13;in fiscal 2016 and 2015, respectively.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;u&gt;Long-Lived Assets&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Long-lived assets such as property and equipment&#13;are stated at their fair value acquisition cost and reviewed for impairment whenever facts and circumstances indicate that the&#13;carrying value may not be recoverable. Amortization of long-lived assets are calculated by the straight line method over their&#13;estimated useful lives. When required impairment losses on assets to be held and used are recognized based on the fair value of&#13;the asset. The fair value is determined based on estimates of future cash flows, market value of similar assets, if available,&#13;or independent appraisals, if required. If the carrying amount of the long-lived asset is not recoverable from its undiscounted&#13;cash flows, an impairment loss is recognized for the difference between the carrying amount and fair value of the asset. When fair&#13;values are not available, the Company estimates fair value using the expected future cash flows discounted at a rate commensurate&#13;with the risk associated with the recovery of the assets.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Depreciation is computed for financial statement&#13;purposes on a straight-line basis over estimated useful lives of the related assets. The estimated useful lives of depreciable&#13;assets are:&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;table cellspacing=0 cellpadding=0 style=width: 100%; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal&gt;&#13;&lt;tr&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=width: 75%&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom; width: 5%; font: 12pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=width: 20%; font: 12pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; text-align: center&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 10pt&gt;&lt;b&gt;Estimated&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&#13;&lt;tr&gt;&#13;    &lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom; font: 12pt Times New Roman

 Serif; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=border-bottom-style: solid; border-bottom-width: 1pt; font: 12pt Times New Roman

 Serif; text-align: center&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 10pt&gt;&lt;b&gt;Useful Lives&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&#13;&lt;tr style=background-color: #CCEEFF&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: top; font: 12pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 10pt&gt;Equipment&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom; font: 12pt Times New Roman

 Serif; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=font: 12pt Times New Roman

 Serif; text-align: center&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 10pt&gt;5-10 years&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&#13;&lt;/table&gt;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;For federal income tax purposes, depreciation&#13;is computed under the modified accelerated cost recovery system. For financial statements purposes, depreciation is computed under&#13;the straight-line method.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;As of May 31, 2016, equipment of $395,195 reflects&#13;acquisition costs. During the year ended May 31, 2016, depreciation is not being calculated as equipment is currently not in use.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;u&gt;Fair Value of Financial Instruments&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company's financial instruments consist&#13;primarily of cash, prepaid expense, deferred financing cost, accounts payable and accrued liabilities, accrued expenses, convertible&#13;notes and Note payable. The carrying amounts of such financial instruments approximate their respective estimated fair value due&#13;to the short-term maturities and approximate market interest rates of these instruments.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company adopted ASC Topic 820, Fair Value&#13;Measurements (&amp;#34;ASC Topic 820&amp;#34;), which defines fair value, establishes a framework for measuring fair value, and expands&#13;disclosures about fair value measurements. The standard provides a consistent definition of fair value which focuses on an exit&#13;price that would be received upon sale of an asset or paid to transfer a liability in an orderly transaction between market participants&#13;at the measurement date. The standard also prioritizes, within the measurement of fair value, the use of market-based information&#13;over entity specific information and establishes a three-level hierarchy for fair value measurements based on the nature of inputs&#13;used in the valuation of an asset or liability as of the measurement date.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The three-level hierarchy for fair value measurements&#13;is defined as follows:&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Level 1 &amp;#150; inputs to the valuation methodology&#13;are quoted prices (unadjusted) for identical assets or liabilities in active markets; liabilities in active markets;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Level 2 &amp;#150; inputs to the valuation methodology&#13;include quoted prices for similar assets and liabilities in active markets, and inputs that are observable for the asset or liability&#13;other than quoted prices, either directly or indirectly, including inputs in markets that are not considered to be active; or directly&#13;or indirectly including inputs in markets that are not considered to be active;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;Level 3 &amp;#150; inputs to the valuation methodology&#13;are unobservable and significant to the fair value measurement&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The following table summarizes fair value measurements&#13;by level at May 31, 2016, and 2015, measured at fair value on a recurring basis:&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;table cellspacing=0 cellpadding=0 style=font: 12pt Times New Roman
 Times

   &lt;td style=text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td colspan=2 style=border-bottom: black 1pt solid; text-align: center&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 10pt&gt;&lt;b&gt;Total&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&#13;&lt;tr&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: top; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 10pt&gt;&lt;b&gt;Liabilities&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td colspan=2 style=vertical-align: bottom;    &lt;td colspan=2 style=vertical-align: bottom; text-align: right&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&#13;&lt;tr style=background-color: #CCEEFF&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: top; width: 389px; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 10pt&gt;Derivative liabilities&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom; text-align: right&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 10pt&gt;-&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom; text-align: right&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 10pt&gt;-&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom; text-align: right&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 10pt&gt;221,040&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom; text-align: right&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 10pt&gt;221,040&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&#13;&lt;tr&gt;&#13;    &lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&#13;&lt;/table&gt;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;u&gt;Basic Earnings (Loss) Per Share&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company computes net income (loss) per&#13;share in accordance with Accounting Standards Codification (&amp;#147;ASC&amp;#148;) 260, &amp;#34;&lt;i&gt;Earnings per Share&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#34;. ASC&#13;260 requires presentation of both basic and diluted earnings per share (EPS) on the face of the income statement. Basic EPS is&#13;computed by dividing net income (loss) available to common shareholders (numerator) by the weighted average number of shares outstanding&#13;(denominator) during the period. Diluted EPS gives effect to all dilutive potential common shares outstanding during the period&#13;using the treasury stock method and convertible preferred stock using the if-converted method. In computing diluted EPS, the average&#13;stock price for the period is used in determining the number of shares assumed to be purchased from the exercise of stock options&#13;or warrants. Diluted EPS excludes all dilutive potential shares if their effect is anti-dilutive.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;u&gt;Recently Issued Accounting Pronouncements&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In November 2015, the FASB issued (ASU) 2015-17,&#13;&amp;#147;Balance Sheet Classification of Deferred Taxes.&amp;#148; Currently deferred taxes for each tax jurisdiction are presented&#13;as a net current asset or liability and net noncurrent asset or liability on the balance sheet. To simplify the presentation, the&#13;new guidance requires that deferred tax liabilities and assets for all jurisdictions along with any related valuation allowances&#13;be classified as noncurrent in a classified statement of financial position. This guidance is effective for interim and annual&#13;reporting periods beginning after December 15, 2016, and early adoption is permitted. The Company has adopted this guidance in&#13;the fourth quarter of the year ended December 31, 2015 on a retrospective basis. The adoption of this guidance did not have a material&#13;impact on the Company&amp;#146;s financial position, results of operations or cash flows, and did not have any effect on prior periods&#13;due to the full valuation allowance against the Company&amp;#146;s net deferred tax assets.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;i&gt;Recent Accounting Pronouncements Issued&#13;But Not Adopted as of May 31, 2016&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In March 2016, the FASB issued ASU 2016-09,&#13;&amp;#147;Compensation - Stock Compensation (Topic 718): Improvements to Employee Share-Based Payment Accounting&amp;#148;. The amendments&#13;are effective for public companies for annual periods beginning after December 15, 2016, and interim periods within those annual&#13;periods. Several aspects of the accounting for share-based payment award transactions are simplified, including: (a) income tax&#13;consequences; (b) classification of awards as either equity or liabilities; and (c) classification on the statement of cash flows.&#13;The Company is currently in the process of evaluating the impact of the adoption on its financial statements.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In February 2016, the FASB issued ASU No. 2016-02,&#13;&amp;#147;Leases (Topic 842)&amp;#148; (&amp;#147;ASU 2016-02&amp;#148;). ASU 2016-02 requires an entity to recognize assets and liabilities&#13;arising from a lease for both financing and operating leases. The ASU will also require new qualitative and quantitative disclosures&#13;to help investors and other financial statement users better understand the amount, timing, and uncertainty of cash flows arising&#13;from leases. ASU 2016-02 is effective for fiscal years beginning after December 15, 2018, with early adoption permitted. The Company&#13;is currently evaluating the impact of adopting this guidance.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In January 2016, the FASB issued ASU 2016-01,&#13;which amends the guidance in U.S. GAAP on the classification and measurement of financial instruments. Changes to the current guidance&#13;primarily affect the accounting for equity investments, financial liabilities under the fair value option, and the presentation&#13;and disclosure requirements for financial instruments. In addition, the ASU clarifies guidance related to the valuation allowance&#13;assessment when recognizing deferred tax assets resulting from unrealized losses on available-for-sale debt securities. The new&#13;standard is effective for fiscal years and interim periods beginning after December 15, 2017, and upon adoption, an entity should&#13;apply the amendments by means of a cumulative-effect adjustment to the balance sheet at the beginning of the first reporting period&#13;in which the guidance is effective. Early adoption is not permitted except for the provision to record fair value changes for financial&#13;liabilities under the fair value option resulting from instrument-specific credit risk in other comprehensive income. The Company&#13;is currently evaluating the impact of adopting this guidance.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In September 2015, the FASB issued ASU 2015-16,&#13;&amp;#147;Simplifying the Accounting for Measurement &amp;#150;Period Adjustments.&amp;#148; Changes to the accounting for measurement-period&#13;adjustments relate to business combinations. Currently, an acquiring entity is required to retrospectively adjust the balance sheet&#13;amounts of the acquiree recognized at the acquisition date with a corresponding adjustment to goodwill as a result of changes made&#13;to the balance sheet amounts of the acquiree. The measurement period is the period after the acquisition date during which the&#13;acquirer may adjust the balance sheet amounts recognized for a business combination (generally up to one year from the date of&#13;acquisition). The changes eliminate the requirement to make such retrospective adjustments, and, instead require the acquiring&#13;entity to record these adjustments in the reporting period they are determined. The new standard is effective for both public and&#13;private companies for periods beginning after December 15, 2015. The Company is currently evaluating the impact of adopting this&#13;guidance.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In August 2015, the FASB issued ASU No. 2015-14,&#13;Revenue From Contracts With Customers (Topic 606).&amp;#34; The amendments in this ASU defer the effective date of ASU 2014-09. Public&#13;business entities should apply the guidance in ASU 2014-09 to annual reporting periods beginning after December 15, 2017, including&#13;interim reporting periods within that reporting period. Earlier application is permitted only as of annual reporting periods beginning&#13;after December 15, 2016, including interim reporting periods within that reporting period. We are still evaluating the effect of&#13;the adoption of ASU 2014-09.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In April 2015, the FASB issued ASU 2015-05,&#13;&amp;#34;Intangibles - Goodwill and Other - Internal-Use Software (Subtopic 350-40): Customer's Accounting for Fees Paid in a Cloud&#13;Computing Arrangement,&amp;#34; which provides guidance about whether a cloud computing arrangement includes a software license. If&#13;a cloud computing arrangement includes a software license, the customer should account for the software license element of the&#13;arrangement consistent with the acquisition of other software licenses. If a cloud computing arrangement does not include a software&#13;license, the customer should account for the arrangement as a service contract. This ASU is effective for annual periods, including&#13;interim periods within those annual periods, beginning after December 15, 2015, and early adoption is permitted. The Company is&#13;currently evaluating the impact of adopting this guidance.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In April 2015, the FASB issued guidance related&#13;to a customer&amp;#146;s accounting for fees paid in a cloud computing arrangement. This standard provides guidance to customers about&#13;whether a cloud computing arrangement includes a software license. If a cloud computing arrangement includes a software license,&#13;then the customer should account for the software license element of the arrangement consistent with the acquisition of other software&#13;licenses. If a cloud computing arrangement does not include a software license, the customer should account for the arrangement&#13;as a service contract. This guidance is effective for interim and annual reporting periods beginning after December 15, 2015, and&#13;early adoption is permitted. The Company will adopt this guidance on January 1, 2016. The adoption of this guidance is not expected&#13;to have a material impact on its financial position, results of operations or cash flows.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company's financial statements are prepared&#13;using accounting principles generally accepted in the United States of America applicable to a going concern, which contemplates&#13;the realization of assets and liquidation of liabilities in the normal course of business. However, the Company has negative working&#13;capital, recurring losses, and does not have an established source of revenues sufficient to cover its operating costs. These factors&#13;raise substantial doubt about the Company&amp;#146;s ability to continue as a going concern.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The ability of the Company to continue as a&#13;going concern is dependent upon its ability to successfully accomplish the plan described in the preceding paragraph and eventually&#13;attain profitable operations. The accompanying financial statements do not include any adjustments that may be necessary if the&#13;Company is unable to continue as a going concern.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;In the coming year, the Company&amp;#146;s foreseeable&#13;cash requirements will relate to continual development of the operations of its business, maintaining its good standing and making&#13;the requisite filings with the Securities and Exchange Commission, and the payment of expenses associated with operations and business&#13;developments. The Company may experience a cash shortfall and be required to raise additional capital.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company sold product to 1PM Industries&#13;and received $30,000 prior to shipment and delivery of the goods and as of May 31, 2015 had delivered goods of $750.&amp;#160;1PM Industries&#13;is developing various gourmet food products such as the development of compound butter and pancake and waffle syrup. The Company&#13;delivered partial shipment on February 28, 2015 to allow 1PM to begin testing different shipping methods related to the product.&#13;During the year ended May 31, 2016, the Company delivered the rest of goods and recognized revenue of $29,250.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

   &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom; border-bottom-style: double; border-bottom-width: 2.25pt; text-align: right&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 10pt&gt;2,022,262&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom; &lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;We did not provide any current or deferred&#13;U.S. federal income tax provision or benefit for any of the periods presented because we have experienced operating losses since&#13;inception. When it is more likely than not that a tax asset cannot be realized through future income the Company must allow for&#13;this future tax benefit. We provided a full valuation allowance on the net deferred tax asset, consisting of net operating loss&#13;carry forwards, because management has determined that it is more likely than not that we will not earn income sufficient to realize&#13;the deferred tax assets during the carry forward period.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company has not taken a tax position that,&#13;if challenged, would have a material effect on the financial statements for the years ended June 2012 applicable under FASB ASC&#13;740. We did not recognize any adjustment to the liability for uncertain tax position and therefore did not record any adjustment&#13;to the beginning balance of accumulated deficit on the balance sheet. All tax returns for the Company remain open.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

   &lt;td style=text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td colspan=2 style=border-bottom-style: solid; border-bottom-width: 1pt;    &lt;td colspan=2 style=vertical-align: bottom; text-align: right&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&#13;&lt;tr style=background-color: #CCEEFF&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: top; width: 569px; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 10pt&gt;Net operating loss carry forward&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 10pt&gt;$&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom; text-align: right&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 10pt&gt;2,928,046&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;font style=font-size: 10pt&gt;$&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=vertical-align: bottom;
